Tuggs later served the buns at his mobile [restaurant](/wiki/Tuggs%27_Grub "Tuggs' Grub") on the Outer Rim planet [Batuu](/wiki/Batuu "Batuu") after the [fall](/wiki/Battle_of_Takodana "Battle of Takodana") of his previous [place](/wiki/Takodana_Castle "Takodana Castle") of employment on [Takodana](/wiki/Takodana "Takodana")[[139]](#cite_note-BSOC-139) in 34 ABY.[[43]](#cite_note-Timelines-43)

Although they typically inhabited natural caverns and abandoned mines, Mustafarians built outdoor structures as necessary, including saucer-shaped buildings at and near active mining sites. Their structures were strongly reinforced and armored to protect them from natural disasters, making their larger facilities [fortresslike](/wiki/Fortress "Fortress") in construction and durability.[[24]](#cite_note-SM-24)

The Mustafarian people shared a deep connection with their planet,[[42]](#cite_note-DV21-42) seeking harmony with the natural forces that sculpted their homeworld.[[2]](#cite_note-Galactic_Explorer's_Guide-2) Surrounded by volcanic magma, their culture was tied to the ebbs and flows of the lava on which they lived.[[42]](#cite_note-DV21-42) In the difficult times of the Empire, history and lore of Mustafar lived on in a Mustafarian leader known as the Priestess, who provided guidance and invaluable information to natives and visitors alike.[[140]](#cite_note-Priestess_DB-140) The natives lived in clans,[[2]](#cite_note-Galactic_Explorer's_Guide-2) and members of Father Kkkt's clan spoke of "lifefires" and "endfires" while discussing the arrival of Darth Vader; Kkkt himself used the Force to form a symbol within a lava river, which he interpreted as an omen of the planet's future. The Mustafarians had a strong desire to protect their homeworld, banding together[[42]](#cite_note-DV21-42) on multiple occasions to defend against Imperial forces.[[30]](#cite_note-Tales_5-30) They had a special relationship with the other life on Mustafar; lava fleas were used to jump over lava flows in a rite of passage, and kahel cave fungi served as the inspiration for Mustafarian architecture.[[13]](#cite_note-CL-13) The Priestess spoke of a being known as [Sleeper](/wiki/Sleeper "Sleeper"), whom she prayed to after encountering a deceased darkghast.[[22]](#cite_note-Immortal_2-22)

 [![The Mustafarians were fierce defenders of their planet.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d9/MustafariansSwarmFortress-TalesFromVadersCastle5.png/revision/latest?cb=20190113171926) [![The Mustafarians were fierce defenders of their planet.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d9/MustafariansSwarmFortress-TalesFromVadersCastle5.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/350?cb=20190113171926)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/d/d9/MustafariansSwarmFortress-TalesFromVadersCastle5.png/revision/latest?cb=20190113171926) 

The Mustafarians were fierce defenders of their planet.

 

Mustafarians were politically organized in accordance with the caverns and communities they inhabited, although they had little in the way of a central government. However, some trusted leaders were allowed to make deals with offworlders in order to help ensure their survival and quality of life. As a result, the Mustafarians fell under the sway of the Techno Union and later the Mining Guild,[[24]](#cite_note-SM-24) serving them as ore scouts, miners, and refinery laborers. While they resented the presence of offworlders,[[2]](#cite_note-Galactic_Explorer's_Guide-2) Mustafarians were generally willing to tolerate a degree of outside political influence as long as it furthered their own cause. Because of the demanding environment of their world, Mustafarians were generally insular and disinterested in galactic affairs, few regarding offworlders with much curiosity. Their focus on the advancement and survival of their own species overrode other concerns, a result of inhabiting a world that demanded so much in order to so much as continue living.[[24]](#cite_note-SM-24)

Mustafarians spoke a [language](/wiki/Language "Language") of the [same name](/wiki/Mustafarian_(language) "Mustafarian (language)"),[[30]](#cite_note-Tales_5-30) which allowed for the precise expression of concepts related to naturals features above and below ground, especially phenomena that were deceptively dangerous. Although the Mustafarian subspecies spoke different dialects, any two individuals could communicate on a functional level despite differing terms and cultural concepts. While they were also capable of speaking [Basic](/wiki/Galactic_Basic_Standard "Galactic Basic Standard") and other common galactic languages, most that did not work with the Mining Guild or deal with outsiders by necessity did not bother to learn Basic. However, Mustafarians that lived or traveled offworld almost always spoke Basic and sometimes the language of their trading partners. Due to their history with the Techno Union, they were more likely to know languages regularly used among former Separatist worlds.[[24]](#cite_note-SM-24)

Mustafarian travels off-world were driven by business pursuits and trade negotiations, and were generally restricted to the Outer Rim. So long as their safety or that of their companions was not threatened, the species was disinterested in galactic affairs, which made them foremost disinclined to leave their homeworld. For Mustafarian merchants and Mining Guild personnel, regular trips were made off-world to trade for upgrades in protective technology and equipment, as well as to deliver ores to buyers. However, there were some Mustafarians who sought full-time employment off-world. They found most inhabited worlds cold, yet relished the relative safety.[[24]](#cite_note-SM-24)

### Invaders and colonizers[]

#### Before the Empire[]

 [![Black Sun's Falleen leadership was based out of Mustafar until the Empire established a garrison on the planet.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/07/BlackSunLeaders-Eminence.png/revision/latest?cb=20131024185422) [![Black Sun's Falleen leadership was based out of Mustafar until the Empire established a garrison on the planet.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/07/BlackSunLeaders-Eminence.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/333?cb=20131024185422)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/0/07/BlackSunLeaders-Eminence.png/revision/latest?cb=20131024185422) 

Black Sun's Falleen leadership was based out of Mustafar until the Empire established a garrison on the planet.

 

The Techno Union, a guild of technology firms led by [Skakoans](/wiki/Skakoan "Skakoan") like [Wat Tambor](/wiki/Wat_Tambor "Wat Tambor"),[[141]](#cite_note-Techno_Union_DB-141) came to value the lucrative minerals of Mustafar and set up operations on the planet.[[13]](#cite_note-CL-13) The offworlders introduced heavy industry, and were welcomed by the native Mustafarians in exchange for access to mining droids and heavy-duty speeders.[[24]](#cite_note-SM-24) However, the natives became subjugated, being put to work in the Techno Union's mining operations[[13]](#cite_note-CL-13) and charged rent on their own planet.[[15]](#cite_note-TROS_VD-15) Management staff of the Union utilized native buildings throughout their operations and provided a refuge for the Separatist Council during the final days of the Clone Wars.[[13]](#cite_note-CL-13) Mining droids used on Mustafar[[4]](#cite_note-ROTS-4) during its time under Techno Union ownership[[34]](#cite_note-CVD-34) included the ore extraction droid, the DLC-13 mining droid, and the electrorefining droid. A number of Separatist battle droids and mouse droids were also present within the facility used by the Separatist Council in the late Clone Wars.[[4]](#cite_note-ROTS-4)

Aside from the native people and the Techno Union, Mustafar was also inhabited by Falleen,[[29]](#cite_note-Eminence-29) tall and muscular [reptomammalians](/wiki/Reptomammal "Reptomammal") native[[142]](#cite_note-HC17-142) to the [Mid Rim](/wiki/Mid_Rim_Territories "Mid Rim Territories")[[5]](#cite_note-TFABG-5) planet of the [same name](/wiki/Falleen_(planet) "Falleen (planet)")[[142]](#cite_note-HC17-142) that controlled the vast Black Sun criminal empire. [Humanoids](/wiki/Humanoid "Humanoid") with distinctly [nonhuman](/wiki/Alien "Alien") appearances, they had ridged [skulls](/wiki/Skeleton "Skeleton"),[[143]](#cite_note-Falleen-143) scaly green skin,[[142]](#cite_note-HC17-142) and exuded powerful [pheromones](/wiki/Pheromone "Pheromone") to attract mates.[[21]](#cite_note-Dark_Disciple-21)

#### Vader's sanctum[]

:   "*We bow only to one, the Dark Lord, the true father and ruler of the galaxy. Vader.*"
:   ―Kylo Ren's translation of an Alazmec warning[[40]](#cite_note-TROS_JN-40)

The Sith Lord Darth Vader called Mustafar his home during the Imperial Era. Originally coming to the planet in hopes of resurrecting his deceased wife,[[42]](#cite_note-DV21-42) Vader lived on the volcanic world for over a decade, utilizing its scorched earth to conduct his personal business,[[19]](#cite_note-Rogue_One-19) and ruled the entire star system[[74]](#cite_note-Kenobi_IV-74) from his castle and its [throne room](/wiki/Vader%27s_throne_room "Vader's throne room").[[84]](#cite_note-Kenobi_III-84) Stories of the Jedi who died by his hand on Mustafar became synonymous with the planet itself.[[87]](#cite_note-Fire_Across_the_Galaxy-87) During his visit to Fortress Vader, Director Krennic theorized that Mustafar was Vader's homeworld, imagining that the Dark Lord's cybernetics were designed to allow him to survive while away from the molten planet.[[16]](#cite_note-Rogue_One_novel-16) The Sith Lord's occupancy was known to others in the galaxy as well. After discovering that Mustafar was Vader's domain, the [Naboo](/wiki/Naboo_(people) "Naboo (people)") resistance group known as the Amidalans deduced that he was responsible for Padmé's death and plotted to kill the Dark Lord to avenge the fallen [queen](/wiki/Monarch_of_Naboo "Monarch of Naboo").[[144]](#cite_note-Vader_2020_3-144)

 [![Darth Vader became the dark lord of Mustafar from his obsidian fortress.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/19/Dv22Gist.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20230815201214) [![Darth Vader became the dark lord of Mustafar from his obsidian fortress.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/19/Dv22Gist.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20230815201214)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/19/Dv22Gist.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20230815201214) 

Darth Vader became the dark lord of Mustafar from his obsidian fortress.

 

As Darth Vader established his personal headquarters on Mustafar, the forces of the Galactic Empire followed.[[42]](#cite_note-DV21-42) Vaneé entered Vader's service as custodian of his castle[[27]](#cite_note-Shadow_of_Vader-27) in 12 BBY,[[43]](#cite_note-Timelines-43) tending to the Sith Lord's daily needs,[[119]](#cite_note-Legacy_of_Vaneé-119) while Admiral Karius served as Vader's second-in-command on the planet[[92]](#cite_note-Karius-92) by 1 BBY.[[43]](#cite_note-Timelines-43) The Imperials' occupation of the planet forced Black Sun[[15]](#cite_note-TROS_VD-15) and the Techno Union to abandon their operations, with the Mining Guild taking over what remained.[[2]](#cite_note-Galactic_Explorer's_Guide-2) Within both Vader's fortress[[30]](#cite_note-Tales_5-30) as well as other installations, the [Imperial Army](/wiki/Imperial_Army "Imperial Army") had a sizable presence on the world,[[91]](#cite_note-Secrets-91) enough that the native population sought to remove them from the planet.[[25]](#cite_note-Return_5-25) Stormtroopers guarded Imperial interests on Mustafar;[[91]](#cite_note-Secrets-91) among their ranks were [magma troopers](/wiki/Magma_trooper "Magma trooper")[[20]](#cite_note-DV23-20) and Lava Troopers, specialized soldiers that operated within the planet's volcanic environment.[[30]](#cite_note-Tales_5-30) M.A.R. Corps of the Rebel Alliance was briefly stationed on Mustafar after being forcibly conscripted by Darth Vader.[[114]](#cite_note-DV202042-114)

Many groups of cultists came to Mustafar in the decades since Vader's passing, seeking the power that the Sith Lord once tapped into on the planet. One of those groups, called the Alazmec of Winsit, gained control of Corvax Fen. They planted several irontrees in its fertile soils in the hopes of restoring the landscape that was once present centuries ago, and were devoted to guarding it from outsiders such as Kylo Ren and the First Order.[[15]](#cite_note-TROS_VD-15) Formed from members of the [Alazmec](/wiki/Alazmec "Alazmec") species, the group wore [night-vision lenses](/wiki/Night-vision_goggles "Night-vision goggles") and weather-resistant [ponchos](/wiki/Poncho "Poncho").[[133]](#cite_note-CEUEE-133)

### Other inhabitants[]

:   "*Lady Corvax abided here with her husband Sir Dorwin, living in peace with my people.*"
:   ―The Priestess speaks to the descendant of Lady Corvax[[14]](#cite_note-Immortal_1-14)

 [![Lady Corvax was responsible for Mustafar's devastation.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/1d/Lady_Corvax.png/revision/latest?cb=20190529173531) [![Lady Corvax was responsible for Mustafar's devastation.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/1d/Lady_Corvax.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/220?cb=20190529173531)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/1d/Lady_Corvax.png/revision/latest?cb=20190529173531) 

Lady Corvax was responsible for Mustafar's devastation.

 

In the planet's vibrant past, the Mustafarians shared the world with Lady Corvax and her husband Dorwin, humanoids who lived peacefully with the natives. Dorwin fell in battle,[[14]](#cite_note-Immortal_1-14) but he did not die; instead, he was cursed to exist between life and death on the ruined world[[22]](#cite_note-Immortal_2-22) until he was freed by Corvax's descendant.[[38]](#cite_note-Immortal_3-38)

The ancient Sith established a presence on Mustafar, hoping to reap the benefits of the dark world and obtain immortality.[[15]](#cite_note-TROS_VD-15) At some point, the Sith Lord Momin found himself on Mustafar, and later, during the Imperial Era, recalled that long ago time.[[73]](#cite_note-DV22-73)

Two mysterious beings resided in a lava cavern near Fortress Vader[[100]](#cite_note-Vader_2020_8-100)—the [spider](/wiki/Spider "Spider")-like Eye of Webbish Bog atop a [blind giant](/wiki/Unidentified_blind_Arobernos "Unidentified blind Arobernos"), who were submerged in their lair and were locked in a symbiotic relationship. Their lair became a small lake beside the Corvax Fen, and they guarded the path to the ruins of Vader's castle.[[44]](#cite_note-TROS_EE-44) Spoken of in the myths of the Mustafarians, the Eye was defended by the Alazmec of Winsit.[[40]](#cite_note-TROS_JN-40)

## Locations[]

It is requested that this article section [be expanded](/wiki/Special:EditPage/:Mustafar "Special:EditPage/:Mustafar"). *Please improve it in any way that you see fit, and remove this notice once the article section is more complete.*

### Settlements[]

:   **Vos**: "*Where can we get a drink?*"
:   **Mustafarian**: "*The Last Resort.*"
:   **Ventress**: "*That the best bar in town?*"
:   **Mustafarian**: "Only *bar in town.*"
:   ―Quinlan Vos and Asajj Ventress ask a local for directions in Zitontown[[21]](#cite_note-Dark_Disciple-21)

The native Mustafarian populace, including both the Northern and Southern sub-species, took up residence in underground caves that were made by lava fleas munching through Mustafar's crust.[[31]](#cite_note-AEYNK-31) Despite this, the two peoples lived in distinct underground cave systems, which resulted in their evolution into two sub-species.[[15]](#cite_note-TROS_VD-15) The Mustafarians' underground buildings were designed in the shape of kahel cave fungus,[[31]](#cite_note-AEYNK-31) which was highly symbolic in Mustafarian culture.[[13]](#cite_note-CL-13)

 [![A mining complex dots the molten surface of Mustafar.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/e0/Complex.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20080218041754) [![A mining complex dots the molten surface of Mustafar.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/e0/Complex.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/280?cb=20080218041754)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/e/e0/Complex.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20080218041754) 

A mining complex dots the molten surface of Mustafar.

 

Due to the planet's fiery surface, outdoor structures were built where necessary—usually at and near active mining sites[[24]](#cite_note-SM-24)—and buildings on Mustafar were held up by stem-like gravity supports.[[31]](#cite_note-AEYNK-31) Its capital [city](/wiki/City "City") was [Fralideja](/wiki/Fralideja "Fralideja"), one of the few remaining Mustafarian settlements at the time of the Clone Wars. A cataclysmic eruption that occurred centuries before the war's end almost destroyed the entire local population. The city and its surrounding structures were of Mustafarian architecture: mushroom-like structures with a habitation dome raised from the scorched ground, based on the shape of the local culture's highly symbolic kahel cave fungus.[[13]](#cite_note-CL-13) The saucer-shaped structures were strongly reinforced and armored against natural calamities, with larger facilities on Mustafar becoming fortresslike in construction and durability.[[24]](#cite_note-SM-24) Although Fralideja and its surrounding buildings that numbered several appeared modular, the structures varied in size and elevation.[[13]](#cite_note-CL-13)

Another settlement was a mining town[[21]](#cite_note-Dark_Disciple-21) known as Zitontown,[[2]](#cite_note-Galactic_Explorer's_Guide-2) named for Ziton Moj, a senior Black Sun [Vigo](/wiki/Vigo "Vigo") who rose to leadership of the organization during the Clone Wars.[[145]](#cite_note-HC39-145) Located outside of town was a fortified[[21]](#cite_note-Dark_Disciple-21) cliffside facility[[146]](#cite_note-Episode_Gallery-146) that served as the organization's headquarters during the conflict.[[58]](#cite_note-BS_DB-58) The installation's architecture was distinct from other facilities located on Mustafar.[[147]](#cite_note-Trivia_Gallery-147) Miners from a variety of species lived and worked in Zitontown, most of whom were poorly nourished in comparison to the Falleen that inhabited the Black Sun fortress. In addition to the fortress, Moj also possessed a palace.[[21]](#cite_note-Dark_Disciple-21)

### Structures and installations[]

:   "*Few people have the honor of seeing Lord Vader in his sanctum. I suggest you keep all you witnessed to yourself.*"
:   ―Vaneé, to Orson Krennic, upon the latter's arrival at Fortress Vader[[16]](#cite_note-Rogue_One_novel-16)

 [![Darth Vader's Fortress on Mustafar](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/64/FortressVader-RogueOneWidevision-SWCT.png/revision/latest?cb=20251208043418) [![Darth Vader's Fortress on Mustafar](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/64/FortressVader-RogueOneWidevision-SWCT.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/280?cb=20251208043418)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/6/64/FortressVader-RogueOneWidevision-SWCT.png/revision/latest?cb=20251208043418) 

Darth Vader's Fortress on Mustafar

 

During the Clone Wars, Darth Sidious secretly maintained an old mining outpost on Mustafar, planning to use the facility to train Force-sensitive children to become his agents. The Sith tasked the bounty hunter Cad Bane with kidnapping children and delivering them to the facility for their training. However, it was destroyed by Sidious' crew of nanny droids after Anakin Skywalker and Ahsoka Tano rescued multiple kidnapped children from the facility.[[17]](#cite_note-Children_of_the_Force-17)

Mustafar was famous for its metal mines,[[148]](#cite_note-Journey_Through_Space_(2015)-148) and was typically used by [spacers](/wiki/Spacer "Spacer") to refuel their vessels.[[17]](#cite_note-Children_of_the_Force-17) The Techno Union maintained multiple mining operations on Mustafar, including a complex built into a lava-filled mountain—which also housed a secret battle droid factory—and a nearby residence for [technicians](/wiki/Technician "Technician") and mine management staff located opposite to the capital city Fralideja. Around the area was a molten rock plain with erupting lava geysers that were repressed by the facility's repulsor fields. In addition to containing a secret command facility, the structure served as cover for a Techno Union droid [production operation](/wiki/Factory "Factory") concealed inside the mountain upon which the mine sat, manufacturing battle droids[[13]](#cite_note-CL-13) for the Separatist Droid Army.[[24]](#cite_note-SM-24) The repulsor fields that protected the complex were inadvertently deactivated during the duel between Obi-Wan Kenobi and Darth Vader and the facility soon fell into ruin.[[13]](#cite_note-CL-13)

 [![Fortress Vader and an Imperial base](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/40/Mustafar-ImpGarrison.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20230625130452) [![Fortress Vader and an Imperial base](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/40/Mustafar-ImpGarrison.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20230625130452)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/40/Mustafar-ImpGarrison.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20230625130452) 

Fortress Vader and an Imperial base

 

Fortress Vader was an obsidian tower built by Lord Momin and Darth Vader as the latter's personal retreat on the Gahenn Plains during the Imperial Era.[[149]](#cite_note-Vader's_castle_DB-149) With a gap dividing the central body of the tower in the middle that resembled tuning forks, the fortress harnessed the surrounding lava for energy. It was also designed to channel the dark side's power,[[12]](#cite_note-Mustafar_DB-12) and, along with being near the site of the Sith Lord's duel against his former master Obi-Wan Kenobi,[[149]](#cite_note-Vader's_castle_DB-149) it was located above an ancient Sith cave to provide a more powerful locus of the dark side for Darth Vader to draw upon.[[12]](#cite_note-Mustafar_DB-12) It was also on the site of the underground fortress of Lady Corvax.[[14]](#cite_note-Immortal_1-14) When visiting the fortress, Imperial officers were intimidated by the surrounding environments, and the treacherous landscape of Mustafar worked to remind them of their place.[[55]](#cite_note-USWNE-55) Vader's castle had an Imperial base in its vicinity, which housed a part of the garrison protecting Vader's sanctum.[[91]](#cite_note-Secrets-91)

### Other landmarks[]

:   "*Mustafar is not like other planets. It is* unique*. Deep beneath its surface rests a locus for the* dark side *of the Force.*"
:   ―Darth Sidious, to Darth Vader[[37]](#cite_note-DV5-37)

 [![The Sith cave housed a powerful heart of darkness.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5e/SithCave-2017DarthVader5.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20170906232344) [![The Sith cave housed a powerful heart of darkness.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5e/SithCave-2017DarthVader5.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/250?cb=20170906232344)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/5/5e/SithCave-2017DarthVader5.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20170906232344) 

The Sith cave housed a powerful heart of darkness.

 

Formerly a part of a Sith temple, the cave beneath Vader's castle contained a locus of the dark side of the Force.[[55]](#cite_note-USWNE-55) The walls of the cave were covered in glowing runic symbols, which Vader and Momin later rearranged to focus the energies of the planet. By tapping into the dark powers of the locus, an individual could open a rift between time and space to enter a portal through the Force.[[78]](#cite_note-DV24-78) Darth Vader also forged his first red lightsaber at the cave, and [Snoke](/wiki/Snoke "Snoke"), the First Order Supreme Leader who trained Kylo Ren, wore a [ring](/wiki/Snoke%27s_ring "Snoke's ring") that featured obsidian carved from the same cave.[[55]](#cite_note-USWNE-55)

Corvax Fen was a vaguely hospitable bog that contained irontrees, being one of Mustafar's few such places. Located close to the ruins of Darth Vader's fortress, the fen was guarded by the Alazmec of Winsit, a group of cultists devoted to the Sith Lord.[[150]](#cite_note-Corvax_Fen_DB-150) Barren and noxious, the marsh was surrounded by a misty air that smelt of [ozone](/wiki/Ozone "Ozone"). It contained a shallow lake of brackish water that was covered in an [oily](/wiki/Oil "Oil") film.[[44]](#cite_note-TROS_EE-44)

## Behind the scenes[]

### Early conception[]

:   "*It was a whole part of the plot that essentially got cut out. It may be in one of the sequels.* […] *Ben and Vader have a confrontation, just like they have in* Star Wars*, and Ben almost kills Vader. As a matter of fact, he falls into a volcanic pit and gets fried and is one destroyed being.*"
:   ―George Lucas on August 25, 1977, the earliest known mention of what would become Mustafar[[151]](#cite_note-Rolling_Stone-151)

 [![Concept art of the Emperor's Throne Room situated above a lava lake, by Ralph McQuarrie](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8b/RMQ-TheLavaThrone-RotJAVA.png/revision/latest?cb=20250316033136) [![Concept art of the Emperor's Throne Room situated above a lava lake, by Ralph McQuarrie](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8b/RMQ-TheLavaThrone-RotJAVA.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/342?cb=20250316033136)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/8/8b/RMQ-TheLavaThrone-RotJAVA.png/revision/latest?cb=20250316033136) 

Concept art of the Emperor's Throne Room situated above a lava lake, by Ralph McQuarrie

 

By [August 25](/wiki/August_25 "August 25"), [1977](/wiki/1977 "1977"), [George Lucas](/wiki/George_Lucas "George Lucas") conceptualized Darth Vader's transformation into a cyborg happening after a duel with Ben Kenobi and the father of Luke Skywalker. The father is killed by Vader, who is confronted and nearly killed by Kenobi. Vader falls into a volcanic pit and is severely injured, necessitating his use of cybernetics.[[151]](#cite_note-Rolling_Stone-151) The concept of a lava duel was revisited in the earliest versions of *Return of the Jedi*. In those versions, Luke Skywalker fights Darth Vader over a lava lake in the [Emperor's Throne Room](/wiki/Emperor%27s_Throne_Room "Emperor's Throne Room"), located in a cave in the lowest levels of the Imperial capital [Had Abbadon](/wiki/Had_Abbadon "Had Abbadon"). Although this was visualized by veteran *Star Wars* concept artist [Ralph McQuarrie](/wiki/Ralph_McQuarrie "Ralph McQuarrie"), the concept was not carried over to the final script.[[152]](#cite_note-Making_of_ROTJ-152) The concept of Kenobi dueling Vader, while altered with Skywalker's father now being Vader himself, was realized in [*Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_III_Revenge_of_the_Sith "Star Wars: Episode III Revenge of the Sith"), twenty-eight years after the original film.[[4]](#cite_note-ROTS-4)

### *Revenge of the Sith*[]

#### Symbolism and naming[]

:   "*Mufasta's been around for a long time. I've always had this set piece: the end between Obi-Wan and Anakin. I knew that's where this movie was going to end up. It's all this volcanic land, with lava shooting up, so it's almost monochromatic in its red-and-blackness. I've had that image with me for a long time.*"
:   ―George Lucas on Mustafar, known as "Mufasta" at that point in the production of *Revenge of the Sith*[[153]](#cite_note-Making_of_RotS-153)

 [![Mustafar was a major setting in Revenge of the Sith](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/17/MustafarHellscape-SWBC52.png/revision/latest?cb=20231221232118) [![Mustafar was a major setting in Revenge of the Sith](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/17/MustafarHellscape-SWBC52.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/350?cb=20231221232118)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/17/MustafarHellscape-SWBC52.png/revision/latest?cb=20231221232118) 

Mustafar was a major setting in *Revenge of the Sith*

 

Released in [2005](/wiki/2005 "2005"), *Revenge of the Sith* marked the first appearance of Mustafar.[[4]](#cite_note-ROTS-4) Brought up as a major location of the film, the volcano world becomes the culmination of the lava designs from the development of the original trilogy. Whilst the planet is named "Mufasta" in earlier concepts for *Revenge of the Sith*, the finalized spelling was in place by [October 25](/wiki/October_25 "October 25"), [2002](/wiki/2002 "2002"); George Lucas had decided to dedicate about twenty to thirty minutes screen time to the planet he respelled, and planned to include a major fight as well as a "love scene" there. Despite the new spelling, draftspeople and model-makers working on the film in [Sydney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sydney "wikipedia:Sydney"), [Australia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia "wikipedia:Australia") spelt the planet name as "Mustafa" when labelling an early 3-D rendering of the lava world's Separatist war room.[[153]](#cite_note-Making_of_RotS-153) "Mustafa," [romanized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romanization "wikipedia:Romanization") from the [Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic "wikipedia:Arabic") (أَلْمُصْطَفَى), is an [epithet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Names_and_titles_of_Muhammad "wikipedia:Names and titles of Muhammad") of [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad "wikipedia:Muhammad") in the [Qur'an](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quran "wikipedia:Quran") that means "The Chosen."[[154]](#cite_note-Quran-154)

Writer-director George Lucas intended the lava planet to symbolize the [Biblical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bible "wikipedia:Bible") [hell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hell "wikipedia:Hell").[[155]](#cite_note-Hell-155) The color scheme of the planet's wilderness was emblematic of the anger and regret that fueled the duel between Skywalker and Kenobi, with the fires and lava floes visualizing the characters' feelings and the conflict between them.[[156]](#cite_note-Insider_216-156) Lucas also said that Anakin Skywalker's injuries that were inflicted by Mustafar led to the loss of his power in the Force; Darth Sidious' plan for his new apprentice to become more powerful than himself was derailed by Obi-Wan Kenobi.[[157]](#cite_note-GL_story-157)

#### Concept art[]

Before Lucasfilm artists finished work on the [2002](/wiki/2002 "2002") prequel trilogy film, [*Star Wars*: Episode II *Attack of the Clones*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_II_Attack_of_the_Clones "Star Wars: Episode II Attack of the Clones"), George Lucas wanted ideas of what his lava planet for Episode III would look like.[[158]](#cite_note-Church_tweet1-158) Prequel trilogy concept artist [Doug Chiang](/wiki/Doug_Chiang "Doug Chiang") had previous made sketches of Mustafar's volcanoes, as well as a castle on the world.[[159]](#cite_note-ROTS_doc-159) The Episode III art department began working in early 2002,[[160]](#cite_note-Art_Dep-160) and at [Skywalker Ranch](/wiki/Skywalker_Ranch "Skywalker Ranch"), artists conceptualized Lucas' lava planet as either a technologically advanced world or a wild, primordial location.[[161]](#cite_note-Featurette-161)

Concept Design Supervisor [Ryan Church](/wiki/Ryan_Church "Ryan Church") made concepts of both using [Corel Painter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corel_Painter "wikipedia:Corel Painter"),[[158]](#cite_note-Church_tweet1-158) and one such piece[[161]](#cite_note-Featurette-161) featured [Gothic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gothic_architecture "wikipedia:Gothic architecture") constructs of skyscraper proportions.[[162]](#cite_note-Church_tweet2-162) When Lucas was shown one of Church's more abstract and fanciful concepts for Mustafar, the director said that he wanted a more grounded design.[[163]](#cite_note-Church_tweet3-163)

The concept artists who worked on Mustafar for Episode III include Concept Design Supervisors Ryan Church and [Erik Tiemens](/wiki/Erik_Tiemens "Erik Tiemens"), [Aaron McBride](/wiki/Aaron_McBride "Aaron McBride"),[[153]](#cite_note-Making_of_RotS-153) and [Derek Thompson](/wiki/Derek_Thompson "Derek Thompson"),[[164]](#cite_note-Thompson-164) amongst others.[[160]](#cite_note-Art_Dep-160) McBride originally designed the [Pau'ans](/wiki/Pau%27an "Pau'an") seen in the final film as natives of Mustafar, although Lucas decided to use his designs for the residents of [Utapau](/wiki/Utapau "Utapau") by 2004.[[165]](#cite_note-McBride_tweet-165)

After the artists made a variety of concepts, such as controlled mineral-harvesting environments complete with lava dams as well as an orbital ring structure that siphoned energy from the lava world, the two extremes ultimately coalesced into what became of Mustafar: a blend of lava-reliant technology and an untamed hellscape.[[161]](#cite_note-Featurette-161)[[166]](#cite_note-Ryan_Church-166) With Lucas stating that the film would begin with seven battles on seven planets in June of 2002, Church made his ring world concept as a *Star Wars* take on a [Dyson sphere](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dyson_sphere "wikipedia:Dyson sphere").[[167]](#cite_note-Church_tweet4-167) In addition, Church conceptualized a [*Venator*-class Star Destroyer](/wiki/Venator-class_Star_Destroyer "Venator-class Star Destroyer") crashing on the world as a result of a battle overhead[[168]](#cite_note-Mufasta_battle1-168)—he had little knowledge of the plot at the time, and thought that the duel between Kenobi and Skywalker could start on the ship and continue after it crashes on the surface of "Mufasta."[[169]](#cite_note-Mufasta_battle2-169) A [June 17](/wiki/June_17 "June 17") piece by Tiemens depicts several Venators attacking the world.[[170]](#cite_note-Mufasta_battle3-170)

Since Lucas insisted that designs for different worlds be instantly distinguishable, owing to the many new planets introduced in Episode III, Church first made a sketch of a Mustafar chamber without color, dated to [September 26](/wiki/September_26 "September 26"), 2002. While the Episode III artists did not know the function of Mustafar beside the apparent ending when it was made, the piece features an imposing "alien-imperial" throne.[[171]](#cite_note-Mufasta_chamber-171) A later piece by Church conveys the magnitude of the world's dangers by showing various technological apparatus keeping a Mustafar bunker together amid lava dams and lavafalls, with a *Venator*-class Star Destroyer docking at the facility. Dated to [October 3](/wiki/October_3 "October 3") of that year, the concept art still referred to the world as "Mufasta."[[172]](#cite_note-Mufasta_bunker_view-172)

#### Animatics[]

:   "*Our director's come up with a really good idea, which I think we'll probably use. I'm not quite sure how we're gonna do this, but what he wants to do* […] *if they get down to the end and it breaks off so that it goes and lands in a river of lava, and they're on it.*"
:   ―George Lucas, relaying Steven Spielberg's ideas for the duel on Mustafar[[173]](#cite_note-Within_a_Minute-173)

George Lucas revised his drafts for the film as the concept art for Mufasta developed, and left details of the duel between Vader and Kenobi untouched for guest director [Steven Spielberg](/wiki/Steven_Spielberg "Steven Spielberg") to form ideas for, based on concept art approved by Lucas during his meetings with the art department.[[153]](#cite_note-Making_of_RotS-153) During an art department meeting, Lucas relayed Spielberg's idea that Vader and Kenobi fight on an extended arm of a Mustafar facility that would break off and fall into the lava flows below. Another idea involves Vader and Kenobi taking shelter behind a ledge as a screen of embers fly down from a spurt of lava, bouncing around and catching on fire. To explain the arm breaking off the Mustafar facility, the art department suggested to Lucas that the film shows lava melting through the structure.[[159]](#cite_note-ROTS_doc-159) Along with animatics supervisor [Daniel D. Gregoire](/wiki/Daniel_D._Gregoire "Daniel D. Gregoire"), Spielberg helped pre-visualize the Mustafar duel as well as the the Utapau chase scene, both as a favor to Lucas and to learn the latest pre-visualization methods for his own 2005 science fiction film, [*War of the Worlds*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_the_Worlds_(2005_film) "wikipedia:War of the Worlds (2005 film)").[[174]](#cite_note-YBYNE-174)

#### Supporting scenery[]

Having heard news that [Mount Etna](/wiki/Mount_Etna "Mount Etna"), a volcano on the island of [Sicily](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sicily "wikipedia:Sicily") in [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italy "wikipedia:Italy"), was erupting in late October, 2002, George Lucas asked [film producer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Film_producer "wikipedia:Film producer") [Rick McCallum](/wiki/Rick_McCallum "Rick McCallum") to arrange the filming of the ongoing volcanic eruption for Mustafar's imagery. With approval from the Italian government and a local guide, acclaimed [documentary filmmaker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Documentary_film "wikipedia:Documentary film") and [cinematographer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cinematographer "wikipedia:Cinematographer") [Ron Fricke](/wiki/Ron_Fricke "Ron Fricke")[[153]](#cite_note-Making_of_RotS-153) accompanied McCallum at the site for over a week,[[159]](#cite_note-ROTS_doc-159) capturing the bursting lava on a camera rented from a company in [Milan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milan "wikipedia:Milan").[[153]](#cite_note-Making_of_RotS-153)

 [![Brett Northcutt's animated, cycloramic background matte painting of Mustafar.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/4b/Mustafar_matte.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20200731102428) [![Brett Northcutt's animated, cycloramic background matte painting of Mustafar.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/4b/Mustafar_matte.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20200731102428)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/4b/Mustafar_matte.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20200731102428) 

Brett Northcutt's animated, cycloramic background matte painting of Mustafar.

 

Amongst other images, lava fountain elements shot by Fricke were incorporated by[[175]](#cite_note-Matte-175) digital matte artist [Brett Northcutt](/wiki/Brett_Northcutt "Brett Northcutt")[[176]](#cite_note-Brett_Northcutt_ILM-176) at the Digital Environments department[[159]](#cite_note-ROTS_doc-159) into an animated background cyclorama used in *Revenge of the Sith*.[[175]](#cite_note-Matte-175) A mesh of various assets that also included stills of gravel at the [Industrial Light & Magic](/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic "Industrial Light & Magic") parking lot and computer generated images, the matte painting comprised of 25,000 pixels and took several months to make, and served as the backdrop for Mustafar in the film.[[159]](#cite_note-ROTS_doc-159)

#### Photography and editing[]

Principal photography began in [Fox Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fox_Studios_Australia "wikipedia:Fox Studios Australia") in Sydney, Australia on [June 30](/wiki/June_30 "June 30"), [2003](/wiki/2003 "2003").[[153]](#cite_note-Making_of_RotS-153) On [July 13](/wiki/July_13 "July 13"), from Skywalker Ranch, Ryan Church made another Mustafar piece to communicate to various film departments of the layout of the Mustafar duel. The piece gives a general idea of the environment in which it would take place and the direction of the battle.[[177]](#cite_note-Church_tweet5-177)

*Revenge of the Sith*'s main model for Mustafar measured eight meters wide and eleven meters long,[[6]](#cite_note-BMF_17-6) and was used for establishing shots of Mustafar's surface surrounding the mining facility.[[159]](#cite_note-ROTS_doc-159) Resin and paint were added to the model, which was carved from high density foam and had a clear plastic glazing base. Between the rocky elements, the model revealed three channels of the transparent plastic for the flow of simulated lava—which was made from tens of thousands of liters of [methocel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypromellose "wikipedia:Hypromellose") with yellow dye. In order to achieve the effect of oozing, glowing lava, ILM employees such as [Todd Lookinland](/wiki/Todd_Lookinland "Todd Lookinland") initially poured buckets of methocel into the upper end of the model, which they tipped by ten degrees, and placed studio lights of 250,000 [watts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Watt "wikipedia:Watt") beneath the plastic channels that the "lava" through. The thickness of the methocel determined the varying shades of red, orange, and yellow resulting from the creative lighting, and black powdered cork was further sprinkled onto the liquid to simulate rocks being carried by the lava flow. An elaborate pump and filtration was installed to recycle the methocel from the bottom on the model back up to the top, maintaining its steady movement.[[6]](#cite_note-BMF_17-6)

ILM further filmed faux explosions using additional methocel on an outdoor lot, as well as the lava bank at the end of Vader and Kenobi's duel—combined with their main lava flow model, Mustafar's model sequences took ILM eight months to film—the longest model shoot in the company's history. The final visuals of the fighting sequence comprise of multiple motion-control shots of the main model, digital animation,[[6]](#cite_note-BMF_17-6) and close up and action shots of Anakin Skywalker actor, [Hayden Christensen](/wiki/Hayden_Christensen "Hayden Christensen"), and Obi-Wan Kenobi actor, [Ewan McGregor](/wiki/Ewan_McGregor "Ewan McGregor"). George Lucas and editor [Roger Barton](/wiki/Roger_Barton "Roger Barton") further incorporated the Mount Etna footage as both their own frames and as elements within other shots of the Mustafar sequences.[[159]](#cite_note-ROTS_doc-159) When Vader and Kenobi fight on the fallen mining complex arm, the lavafall[[4]](#cite_note-ROTS-4) flows backwards as a result of an edit by George Lucas to ensure the camera follows the duelists in a single direction as they progress.[[159]](#cite_note-ROTS_doc-159)

### *Star Wars: The Clone Wars*[]

:   "*Mustafar was also a big deal for me, 'cause I argued with George about that, I said, 'Really, Mustafar?' Because that's where the whole thing with Vader happens* […] *You find your fan-self clashing with the story that George wants to tell, 'cause we hold everything—'Oh, it's so precious to me, and nobody can know about Mustafar!"* […] *We take it to such this uber-serious level and it always takes George to, you know, snap you out of it sometimes and say, 'But this a great ending to this trilogy* [of episodes]*.'*"
:   ―Dave Filoni, on his initial reluctance to use Mustafar on the show[[178]](#cite_note-CotF_Featurette-178)

An earlier version of the story for the *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")* [Season One](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_One "The Clone Wars: Season One") episode "[Liberty on Ryloth](/wiki/Liberty_on_Ryloth "Liberty on Ryloth")" featured [Mace Windu](/wiki/Mace_Windu "Mace Windu") rescuing [Twi'lek](/wiki/Twi%27lek "Twi'lek") captives from a prison suspended over a volcanic caldera. Although this was cut when production paintings of the setting ended up looking too similar to Mustafar,[[179]](#cite_note-Liberty_on_Ryloth_Trivia_Gallery-179) the location was revived for the [Season Four](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_Four "The Clone Wars: Season Four") episodes "[Slaves of the Republic](/wiki/Slaves_of_the_Republic "Slaves of the Republic")"[[180]](#cite_note-Slaves_of_the_Republic_Trivia_Gallery-180) and "[Escape from Kadavo](/wiki/Escape_from_Kadavo "Escape from Kadavo")" as the [Kadavo slave processing facility](/wiki/Kadavo_slave_processing_facility "Kadavo slave processing facility").[[181]](#cite_note-Escape_from_Kadavo-181)

 [![The symbolic Well of the Dark Side at the ethereal realm of Mortis.](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a7/AnakinSeduced-GOM.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20110215154442) [![The symbolic Well of the Dark Side at the ethereal realm of Mortis.](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a7/AnakinSeduced-GOM.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20110215154442)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/a/a7/AnakinSeduced-GOM.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20110215154442) 

The symbolic Well of the Dark Side at the ethereal realm of Mortis.

 

Mustafar itself made an appearance in the show's [second season](/wiki/The_Clone_Wars:_Season_Two "The Clone Wars: Season Two") episode "[Children of the Force](/wiki/Children_of_the_Force "Children of the Force")," serving as the final destination of a three-part arc in the series.[[17]](#cite_note-Children_of_the_Force-17) Development of the planet for the show was challenging for the *Clone Wars* team, as the lava and explosion visuals required for the episode called for significant effects work. Supervising director [Dave Filoni](/wiki/Dave_Filoni "Dave Filoni") also noted that Mustafar's inclusion in the show was initially difficult for him as a fan; to him, the planet was too important to Anakin's story in *Revenge of the Sith* to be included earlier in the timeline. George Lucas, however, convinced him that Mustafar served as the ideal location for the arc's finale, prompting Filoni to rationalize that the world was not likely to be unknown to the galaxy at large, further reasoning that the planet's perceived significance among fans was superseded by the needs of the story.[[178]](#cite_note-CotF_Featurette-178)

According to effects supervisor [Joel Aron](/wiki/Joel_Aron "Joel Aron"), some of the elements of Mustafar's lava from *Revenge of the Sith* were repurposed for the [Well of the Dark Side](/wiki/Well_of_the_Dark_Side "Well of the Dark Side") on [Mortis](/wiki/Mortis "Mortis") in the episode "[Ghosts of Mortis](/wiki/Ghosts_of_Mortis "Ghosts of Mortis")."[[182]](#cite_note-Ghosts_of_Mortis_Trivia_Gallery-182)

### *Rogue One*[]

:   "*When we established Mustafar as Vader's home for* Rogue One*, we then needed more interiors and a bigger picture. So it was really fun to dig up those old McQuarrie designs, to figure out how to blend them with our aesthetic, as well as the aesthetic from* Revenge of the Sith*.*"
:   ―Doug Chiang on Mustafar's appearance in *Rogue One*[[183]](#cite_note-R1_Art-183)

Mustafar was later featured in the [2016](/wiki/2016 "2016") [*Star Wars* Anthology](/wiki/Star_Wars_Anthology_Series "Star Wars Anthology Series") film, *[Rogue One: A Star Wars Story](/wiki/Rogue_One:_A_Star_Wars_Story "Rogue One: A Star Wars Story")*. It was the site of Fortress Vader, a stronghold where Darth Vader resided.[[19]](#cite_note-Rogue_One-19) To prepare for the planet's return to film, art director Doug Chiang and the design team revisited Ralph McQuarrie's old designs for Mustafar and combined them with its depiction in *Revenge of the Sith* in order to create a unique aesthetic. Fortress Vader was created based off of a few of McQuarrie's designs,[[183]](#cite_note-R1_Art-183) including a series of paintings and sketches of an underground lava cave,[[184]](#cite_note-High_bar-184) with the Emperor's throne on Had Abbadon[[152]](#cite_note-Making_of_ROTJ-152) interpreted instead as Vader's throne in the Sith cave beneath the Dark Lord's castle.[[184]](#cite_note-High_bar-184) It was also designed to look similar to a [tuning fork](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tuning_fork "wikipedia:Tuning fork"), representing the structure being attuned to the Force, a theme also used when designing the [Temple of the Kyber](/wiki/Temple_of_the_Kyber "Temple of the Kyber").[[185]](#cite_note-Tuning_Fork-185) Interior concept designs for what eventually became the stronghold were created by Ryan Church, [Matt Allsopp](/wiki/Matt_Allsopp "Matt Allsopp"), [Luke Fisher](/wiki/Luke_Fisher "Luke Fisher"), [Julian Caldow](/wiki/Julian_Caldow "Julian Caldow"), [Thom Tenery](/wiki/Thom_Tenery "Thom Tenery"), Brett Northcutt, and Erik Tiemens, while the landscape was drawn by Allsopp and [Christian Alzmann](/wiki/Christian_Alzmann "Christian Alzmann").[[183]](#cite_note-R1_Art-183)

### *The Rise of Skywalker*[]

:   "*The one time we weren't in the studio got cut.*"  
    "*Yes. One time we were in a battle scene in a forest, with Kylo Ren. Our bits got cut out, so we have to wait for those on the extras.*"
:   ―Gleeson and Grant speak on their deleted scene[[186]](#cite_note-Gleeson_&_Grant_Interview-186)

 [![Domhnall Gleeson and Richard E](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/ff/Mustafar-TROS-BTS.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20200624061033) [![Domhnall Gleeson and Richard E](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/ff/Mustafar-TROS-BTS.jpg/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/300?cb=20200624061033)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/f/ff/Mustafar-TROS-BTS.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20200624061033) 

Domhnall Gleeson and Richard E. Grant on *The Rise of Skywalker*'s Mustafar set

 

The planet was featured in the opening scene of the [2019](/wiki/2019 "2019") [sequel trilogy](/wiki/Sequel_trilogy "Sequel trilogy") film [*Star Wars*: Episode IX *The Rise of Skywalker*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IX_The_Rise_of_Skywalker "Star Wars: Episode IX The Rise of Skywalker"), in which Kylo Ren leads a First Order attack on Mustafar to obtain a Sith wayfinder. While the final film features only about a minute of screentime for the world,[[137]](#cite_note-Episode_IX-137) additional scenes were originally planned. Actors [Domhnall Gleeson](/wiki/Domhnall_Gleeson "Domhnall Gleeson") and [Richard E. Grant](/wiki/Richard_E._Grant "Richard E. Grant"), who played the First Order leaders Hux and Pryde, respectively, have stated that at one point their characters were meant to accompany Ren to Mustafar. Although the actors did indeed film the scene, it was [removed](/wiki/Content_cut_from_Star_Wars "Content cut from Star Wars") from the final cut of the film. Gleeson and Grant expressed a desire to see the scene released on home media,[[186]](#cite_note-Gleeson_&_Grant_Interview-186) but the footage was never provided.[[137]](#cite_note-Episode_IX-137) A version of this scene was later included in [Rae Carson](/wiki/Rae_Carson "Rae Carson")'s [2020](/wiki/2020 "2020") [novelization](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Rise_of_Skywalker:_Expanded_Edition "Star Wars: The Rise of Skywalker: Expanded Edition") of the film.[[44]](#cite_note-TROS_EE-44)

Another deleted scene, featuring Ren's encounter with the Eye of Webbish Bog on the planet, was filmed near the [United Kingdom's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom "wikipedia:United Kingdom") [Pinewood Studios](/wiki/Pinewood_Studios "Pinewood Studios") in a lake at [Black Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Park "wikipedia:Black Park"). According to creature and special make-up effects creative supervisor [Neal Scanlan](/wiki/Neal_Scanlan "Neal Scanlan"), the scene was cut due to its long length and concerns with conveying information to the audience effectively.[[187]](#cite_note-Eye_Cut-187) This scene also went on to be included in Carson's novelization,[[44]](#cite_note-TROS_EE-44) as well as in [Michael Kogge](/wiki/Michael_Kogge "Michael Kogge")'s [junior novelization](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Rise_of_Skywalker:_A_Junior_Novel "Star Wars: The Rise of Skywalker: A Junior Novel") later that year.[[40]](#cite_note-TROS_JN-40) The two works present different interpretations of the sequence, however. In Carson's book, Ren wades through the Eye's lake to reach a small island and obtain the wayfinder,[[44]](#cite_note-TROS_EE-44) whereas Kogge's adaptation depicts the creature pointing Kylo beyond the lake and towards the remains of Vader's fortress.[[40]](#cite_note-TROS_JN-40) This article assumes neither story has canonical precedence over the other and presents a combined version of these events.

### No mean setting[]

:   "*You can see exotic worlds across the galaxy in the Empire.*"
:   ―A segment of "In the Empire" in which Mustafar appears[[188]](#cite_note-P&F-188)

 [![Mustafar, in Phineas and Ferb: Star Wars](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/49/Mustafar-PnF.png/revision/latest?cb=20230826093253) [![Mustafar, in Phineas and Ferb: Star Wars](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/49/Mustafar-PnF.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/350?cb=20230826093253)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/4/49/Mustafar-PnF.png/revision/latest?cb=20230826093253) 

Mustafar, in *Phineas and Ferb: Star Wars*

 

Mustafar is among the various locations showcased in a montage promoting the [Stormtrooper Corps](/wiki/Stormtrooper_Corps "Stormtrooper Corps") during the stormtrooper [Candace](/wiki/Candace "Candace")'s performance of the song "[In the Empire](/wiki/In_the_Empire "In the Empire")" in the [2014](/wiki/2014 "2014") non-canonical film *[Phineas and Ferb: Star Wars](/wiki/Phineas_and_Ferb:_Star_Wars "Phineas and Ferb: Star Wars")*.[[188]](#cite_note-P&F-188) In the 2020 mobile [video game](/wiki/Star_Wars_video_games "Star Wars video games") *[Star Wars: Starfighter Missions](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Starfighter_Missions "Star Wars: Starfighter Missions")*, Mustafar appears as one of the locations over which starfighter battles take place.[[189]](#cite_note-Starfighter_Missions-189)

### *Obi-Wan Kenobi*[]

In [Stuart Beattie](/wiki/Stuart_Beattie "Stuart Beattie")'s script for a canceled Obi-Wan Kenobi feature film that later evolved into the [2022](/wiki/2022 "2022") *[Star Wars: Obi-Wan Kenobi](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Obi-Wan_Kenobi "Star Wars: Obi-Wan Kenobi")* television series, Kenobi would fall in with [refugees](/wiki/Refugee "Refugee") that are fleeing from the Empire. Tao, the lead refugee woman, takes Kenobi to a sacred shrine and instructs the Jedi Master to let their [goddess](/wiki/Deity "Deity") speak to him. Later on Mustafar, Kenobi experiences a vision in which he is attacked by Luke Skywalker, who almost kills him. Kenobi then realizes that putting his guilt on the young Skywalker would turn himself to the dark side of the Force. The duel was intended to mirror the [dark side cave](/wiki/Cave_of_Evil "Cave of Evil") scene in the [1980](/wiki/1980 "1980") film [*Star Wars*: Episode V *The Empire Strikes Back*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_V_The_Empire_Strikes_Back "Star Wars: Episode V The Empire Strikes Back").[[190]](#cite_note-Cody_Scrapped_Role-190)

First published on [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com") on [June 24](/wiki/June_24 "June 24"), 2022, and written by [Emily Shkoukani](/wiki/Emily_Shkoukani "Emily Shkoukani") of the [Lucasfilm Story Group](/wiki/Lucasfilm_Story_Group "Lucasfilm Story Group"), [*Star Wars Inside Intel: The Inquisitorius*](/wiki/Star_Wars_Inside_Intel "Star Wars Inside Intel") stated the moon of Nur, where the Inquisitorius maintained their base of operations and was featured in the *Obi-Wan Kenobi* series, orbited Mustafar.[[191]](#cite_note-Insider_Intel_old-191) However, in [2023](/wiki/2023 "2023"), the article was updated to remove this, instead more simply stating the moon was located in the Mustafar system.[[192]](#cite_note-Insider_Intel-192) Although the 2023 reference title *[Star Wars: Dawn of Rebellion: The Visual Guide](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Dawn_of_Rebellion:_The_Visual_Guide "Star Wars: Dawn of Rebellion: The Visual Guide")* also states that Nur orbited Mustafar,[[77]](#cite_note-Dawn-77) the 2020 reference title *[The Star Wars Book](/wiki/The_Star_Wars_Book "The Star Wars Book")* simply states that Nur was a moon in the Mustafar system,[[75]](#cite_note-TSWB-75) which this article maintains rather than assume further.

### LEGO media[]

#### Animation[]

:   "*Mustafar. From its violent depths I rose, just as my new castle rises as the ultimate testimony to the awesome power of the dark side! —so, what do you think?*"  
    "*Hmph. A little on the nose, is what I think.*"
:   ―Darth Vader and Darth Sidious, in *LEGO Star Wars Terrifying Tales*[[193]](#cite_note-TerrifyingTales-193)

In the [2015](/wiki/2015 "2015") non-canonical *[LEGO Star Wars: Droid Tales](/wiki/LEGO_Star_Wars:_Droid_Tales "LEGO Star Wars: Droid Tales")* series' "[Crisis on Coruscant](/wiki/Crisis_on_Coruscant "Crisis on Coruscant")" episode, the droid C-3PO recounts the events of *Revenge of the Sith*, including the duel on Mustafar: the fight ends with Obi-Wan Kenobi accidentally pushing Anakin Skywalker straight into lava.[[194]](#cite_note-LEGO_Crisis-194)

In the 2023 non-canonical verbal short "[The Sith Witch of Mustafar](/wiki/The_Sith_Witch_of_Mustafar "The Sith Witch of Mustafar")" of the *[LEGO STAR WARS: Celebrate the Season](/wiki/LEGO_STAR_WARS:_Celebrate_the_Season "LEGO STAR WARS: Celebrate the Season")* animated anthology series, Darth Sidious finds his apprentice at his castle on Mustafar on [Halloween](/wiki/Halloween "Halloween") and complains that he had searched the galaxy for him, and insists that they return to Sidious' shuttle to get on with their work. Vader reluctantly follows his master out of the castle and warns about an alleged "[Sith Witch of Mustafar](/wiki/Sith_Witch_of_Mustafar "Sith Witch of Mustafar")" who haunted Mustafar's spooky landscape. Although Sidious kept dismissing Vader's warnings, they are frightened by signs of the alleged Sith Witch when they walk into the middle of the woods in a swale. However, the Dark Lords discover that they were merely found by stormtroopers dressed up for Halloween, and Sidious allows each trooper to take one Halloween sweet from him. The Sith then continue walking to their shuttle as the troopers leave, but are spooked by R2-D2 dressed up as a ghost. To their distress, the trio subsequently find a great light in the woods.[[195]](#cite_note-Sith_Witch-195)

In "[Mech My Day](/wiki/Mech_My_Day "Mech My Day")," a non-verbal short of the series released on the same day, Vader is annoyed by the clumsiness of one of the [stormtroopers](/wiki/Unidentified_stormtrooper_(mech) "Unidentified stormtrooper (mech)") who were cleaning his throne room in his castle. That stormtrooper constructs a personal [mech suit](/wiki/Stormtrooper_mech "Stormtrooper mech"), showing off the creation to fellow troopers before Vader. The angered Sith Lord builds his own [mech](/wiki/Darth_Vader_Mech "Darth Vader Mech") and battles the stormtrooper, but they are interrupted by the bounty hunter [Boba Fett](/wiki/Boba_Fett "Boba Fett"), arriving from his [ship](/wiki/Slave_I "Slave I") to join the mech fight with his own [mech suit](/wiki/Boba_Fett_Mech "Boba Fett Mech"). Fett destroys Vader and the trooper's mech suits as he flies through the ceiling of Vader's throne room, and the Dark Lord begins to punish the trooper.[[196]](#cite_note-Mech-196)

In the 2020 non-canonical film *[The LEGO Star Wars Holiday Special](/wiki/The_LEGO_Star_Wars_Holiday_Special "The LEGO Star Wars Holiday Special")*, set after the events of *The Rise of Skywalker*[[197]](#cite_note-LEGO_Holiday-197) of 35 ABY,[[43]](#cite_note-Timelines-43) the Jedi [Rey Skywalker](/wiki/Rey_Skywalker "Rey Skywalker") obtains a [key](/wiki/Key "Key") on the planet [Kordoku](/wiki/Kordoku "Kordoku") that allows her to travel through portals in time. Her activation of the key leads to Darth Vader from the past attempting to seize the key for himself, and during his lightsaber duel against Skywalker, the two, along with a pair of [snowtroopers](/wiki/Cold_weather_assault_trooper "Cold weather assault trooper") from the [Battle of Hoth](/wiki/Battle_of_Hoth "Battle of Hoth"), arrive on Mustafar during the duel between Obi-Wan Kenobi and Darth Vader over a river of lava from a portal above. While Rey Skywalker and the Vader in pursuit of her continue their duel over two mining droids, the snowtroopers take the key on a mining platform and attempt to pass it to their commander, but Skywalker intercepts it through the Force. As the group approach a lavafall, Skywalker opens another portal over its crest, and all participants safely enter it and reach a [battle](/wiki/Clash_on_Nevarro "Clash on Nevarro") on the planet [Nevarro](/wiki/Nevarro "Nevarro").[[197]](#cite_note-LEGO_Holiday-197)

The [2021](/wiki/2021 "2021") non-canonical film *[LEGO Star Wars Terrifying Tales](/wiki/LEGO_Star_Wars_Terrifying_Tales "LEGO Star Wars Terrifying Tales")* features Vader's castle on Mustafar, where the Dark Lord boasts of his new sanctum beside Darth Sidious before the pair leave, allowing Vaneé to look after the place in their absence. Later, after the end of the war against the First Order[[193]](#cite_note-TerrifyingTales-193) in 35 ABY,[[43]](#cite_note-Timelines-43) the Resistance pilot General [Poe Dameron](/wiki/Poe_Dameron "Poe Dameron") and his droid companion [BB-8](/wiki/BB-8 "BB-8") make an emergency landing of their faulty [X-wing](/wiki/T-70_X-wing_starfighter "T-70 X-wing starfighter") in an irontree forest on Mustafar. Stranded, the pair enter Fortress Vader and find it being converted into a Sith-themed luxury resort by [Graballa](/wiki/Graballa/LEGO "Graballa/LEGO") the Hutt and his [Iktotchi](/wiki/Iktotchi "Iktotchi") henchmen, [Baash](/wiki/Baash "Baash") and [Raam](/wiki/Raam "Raam"). Dameron then meets the young mechanic [Dean](/wiki/Dean_(mechanic) "Dean (mechanic)"), whom he enlists to fix the [X-wing](/wiki/X-wing_starfighter "X-wing starfighter"), but they are blocked from doing so by Vaneé; he presents the helmet of Ren, who had been Master of the Knights of Ren before Kylo Ren. Working with the Imperial [protocol droid](/wiki/RA-7_protocol_droid "RA-7 protocol droid") [NI-L8](/wiki/NI-L8 "NI-L8"), Vaneé wishes to use Dameron to unlock Vader's treasures, based on a prophecy that foretold a fearless stranger would have the strength to do so.[[193]](#cite_note-TerrifyingTales-193)

After recounting the story of the [rise](/wiki/Destruction_of_the_Jedi_Temple "Destruction of the Jedi Temple") of Kylo Ren, Vaneé, surrounded by [bats](/wiki/Bat "Bat"), leads his guests to a repository of Sith artifacts, finding the [Saber of Scardont](/wiki/Saber_of_Scardont "Saber of Scardont") and recounting its tale. While repairing the saber, Dean is mesmerized by its power and leads the group to the treasure-filled first Temple of Mustafar, unlocking a [Sith holocron](/wiki/Sith_holocron "Sith holocron") as Vaneé delivers a tale of the Death Star. Vaneé then seizes the [holocron](/wiki/Holocron "Holocron") and arms himself and NI-L8 leads an army of [B1-series battle droids](/wiki/B1-series_battle_droid "B1-series battle droid") to attack the rest of the group. At the end of a battle against Dameron, Dean, and BB-8 in the forest and lava flow outside the castle, Dean hurls the holocron away; Vaneé jumps after it and is consumed by the lava below. Afterward, Graballa and his henchmen depart to launch a bed-and-breakfast business, while Dameron offers Dean a place in the Resistance as a pilot and to learn about the Force from Rey Skywalker before they leave with BB-8 as well. In the lava, NI-L8 emerges and is joined by Vaneé.[[193]](#cite_note-TerrifyingTales-193)

#### *The Skywalker Saga*[]

In the 2022 non-canon video game *[LEGO Star Wars: The Skywalker Saga](/wiki/LEGO_Star_Wars:_The_Skywalker_Saga "LEGO Star Wars: The Skywalker Saga")*, Mustafar is one of the worlds that players can freely explore and a setting in the story missions for *Star Wars*: Episode III *Revenge of the Sith*. It is also shown in cutscenes for *Star Wars*: Episode IX *The Rise of Skywalker*.[[198]](#cite_note-TSS-198)

Elsewhere in the game, a [Lanai](/wiki/Lanai "Lanai") [Caretaker](/wiki/Caretakers "Caretakers") wishing to make invulnerable obsidian wheelbarrow on the planet [Ahch-To](/wiki/Ahch-To "Ahch-To")'s [Temple Island](/wiki/Temple_Island "Temple Island") asks the player character to find out where obsidian could be obtained, having been frustrated by the destruction of wheelbarrows during Rey's visit[[198]](#cite_note-TSS-198) in 34 ABY.[[43]](#cite_note-Timelines-43) A [Devaronian](/wiki/Devaronian "Devaronian") in the city [Mos Espa](/wiki/Mos_Espa "Mos Espa") on the planet Tatooine then suggests that obsidian could be found on Mustafar. On the planet [Pasaana](/wiki/Pasaana "Pasaana") during the [Festival of the Ancestors](/wiki/Festival_of_the_Ancestors "Festival of the Ancestors")[[198]](#cite_note-TSS-198) in 35 ABY,[[43]](#cite_note-Timelines-43) an [Aki-Aki Storyteller](/wiki/Aki-Aki_Storyteller "Aki-Aki Storyteller") describes the duel between "Dopi-Won" and "Panakin Slytalker" on an "oven" world to a group of [Aki-Aki](/wiki/Aki-Aki "Aki-Aki") children as part of a puppet play. The stage's backdrop for the scene is a tapestry that depicts the mining facility on Mustafar.[[198]](#cite_note-TSS-198)

As *[Star Wars: Absolutely Everything You Need to Know, Updated and Expanded](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Absolutely_Everything_You_Need_to_Know,_Updated_and_Expanded "Star Wars: Absolutely Everything You Need to Know, Updated and Expanded")* establishes that one [standard day](/wiki/Standard_day "Standard day") was 24 standard hours, Mustafar's orbital period consisted of 14832 standard hours, or 618 [↑](#cite_ref-Star_Wars_11_date_51-0) *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")* dates the [rescue of Luke Skywalker](/wiki/Rescue_of_Luke_Skywalker "Rescue of Luke Skywalker") to [0 ABY](/wiki/0_ABY "0 ABY"). As [Kongo](/wiki/Kongo "Kongo") was said to be the last of his [kind](/wiki/Roggwart "Roggwart") during the rescue of [Luke Skywalker](/wiki/Luke_Skywalker "Luke Skywalker"), it can additionally be determined that he was reputed to be the last of his kind by 0 [ABY](/wiki/%27ABY-BBY%27_dating_system "'ABY-BBY' dating system"). 52. ↑ [52.0](#cite_ref-Beware_the_Nameless_52-0) [52.1](#cite_ref-Beware_the_Nameless_52-1) *[The High Republic: Beware the Nameless](/wiki/The_High_Republic:_Beware_the_Nameless "The High Republic: Beware the Nameless")* 53. ↑ [53.0](#cite_ref-Tales_2_53-0) [53.1](#cite_ref-Tales_2_53-1) [*Star Wars Adventures: Tales from Vader's Castle* 2](/wiki/Star_Wars_Adventures:_Tales_from_Vader%27s_Castle_2 "Star Wars Adventures: Tales from Vader's Castle 2") 54. ↑ [54.0](#cite_ref-Inside_Intel_54-0) [54.1](#cite_ref-Inside_Intel_54-1) [54.2](#cite_ref-Inside_Intel_54-2) [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com") [*Star Wars* Inside Intel: Mustafar](/wiki/Star_Wars_Inside_Intel "Star Wars Inside Intel") on [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com") ([article](https://www.starwars.com/news/star-wars-inside-intel-mustafar)) ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20210831142851/https://www.starwars.com/news/star-wars-inside-intel-mustafar)) 55. ↑ [55.00](#cite_ref-USWNE_55-0) [55.01](#cite_ref-USWNE_55-1) [55.02](#cite_ref-USWNE_55-2) [55.03](#cite_ref-USWNE_55-3) [55.04](#cite_ref-USWNE_55-4) [55.05](#cite_ref-USWNE_55-5) [55.06](#cite_ref-USWNE_55-6) [55.07](#cite_ref-USWNE_55-7) [55.08](#cite_ref-USWNE_55-8) [55.09](#cite_ref-USWNE_55-9) *[Ultimate Star Wars, New Edition](/wiki/Ultimate_Star_Wars,_New_Edition "Ultimate Star Wars, New Edition")* 56. [↑](#cite_ref-Beware_the_Nameless_Date_56-0) *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")* dates [Starlight Beacon's destruction](/wiki/Destruction_of_Starlight_Beacon "Destruction of Starlight Beacon") to [230 BBY](/wiki/230_BBY "230 BBY"). The implementation of the [Guardian Protocols](/wiki/Guardian_Protocols "Guardian Protocols"), which *[Star Wars: The High Republic Character Encyclopedia](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_High_Republic_Character_Encyclopedia "Star Wars: The High Republic Character Encyclopedia")* places in [229 BBY](/wiki/229_BBY "229 BBY"), took place one [week](/wiki/Standard_week "Standard week") after [Starlight Beacon](/wiki/Starlight_Beacon "Starlight Beacon")'s fall according to [*The High Republic – Shadows of Starlight* 1](/wiki/The_High_Republic_%E2%80%93_Shadows_of_Starlight_1 "The High Republic – Shadows of Starlight 1"). As *[The High Republic: Temptation of the Force](/wiki/The_High_Republic:_Temptation_of_the_Force "The High Republic: Temptation of the Force")* takes place one [year](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") and six weeks after the destruction of Starlight Beacon, it must be set in [228 BBY](/wiki/228_BBY "228 BBY"). Since *[The High Republic: Beware the Nameless](/wiki/The_High_Republic:_Beware_the_Nameless "The High Republic: Beware the Nameless")* takes place one year and six [months](/wiki/Standard_month "Standard month") after the destruction of Starlight Beacon, its events must be set in 228 [BBY](/wiki/%27ABY-BBY%27_dating_system "'ABY-BBY' dating system") as well. 57. ↑ [57.0](#cite_ref-M&A_57-0) [57.1](#cite_ref-M&A_57-1) *[Master & Apprentice](/wiki/Master_%26_Apprentice "Master & Apprentice")* 58. ↑ [58.0](#cite_ref-BS_DB_58-0) [58.1](#cite_ref-BS_DB_58-1) [58.2](#cite_ref-BS_DB_58-2) [StarWars-DatabankII](/wiki/Databank_(2014-) "Databank (2014-)") [Black Sun](https://www.starwars.com/databank/black-sun) in the [Databank](/wiki/Databank_(2014-) "Databank (2014-)") ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20170825165811/https://www.starwars.com/databank/black-sun)) 59. [↑](#cite_ref-Ahsoka_date_66-0) The early chapters of the novel [*Ahsoka*](/wiki/Ahsoka_(novel) "Ahsoka (novel)") state that its events take place one [year](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after the [Galactic Empire](/wiki/Galactic_Empire "Galactic Empire")'s [founding](/wiki/Proclamation_of_the_New_Order "Proclamation of the New Order"), which *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")* states was concurrent to the [duel on Mustafar](/wiki/Duel_on_Mustafar "Duel on Mustafar"), dated to [19 BBY](/wiki/19_BBY "19 BBY"). Therefore, the later chapters of *Ahsoka* take place more than a year after the duel, in [18 BBY](/wiki/18_BBY "18 BBY"). 67. [↑](#cite_ref-Hunters_Date_125-0) [ArenaNews-Logo](https://starwarshunters.com) [Hunters Goes Galactic!](https://web.archive.org/web/20241202054735/https://starwarshunters.com/arena-news/11218a292ab549cda65e6cd727f37919-en-gb) on [Arena News](/wiki/Arena_News "Arena News") ([original site](https://starwarshunters.com/arena-news/11218a292ab549cda65e6cd727f37919-en-gb) is defunct) establishes that *[Star Wars: Hunters](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Hunters "Star Wars: Hunters")* begins when the [Grand Arena](/wiki/Grand_Arena "Grand Arena") partnered with the [Outer Rim Sports Network](/wiki/Outer_Rim_Sports_Network "Outer Rim Sports Network"), dated to [9 ABY](/wiki/9_ABY "9 ABY") in *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")*. 126. [↑](#cite_ref-Sentinel_M2_127-0) [StarWarsHunters-Logo](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Hunters "Star Wars: Hunters") *[Star Wars: Hunters](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Hunters "Star Wars: Hunters")* — Story: "Sentinel Mastery II" 128. [↑](#cite_ref-Skeleton_Crew_Date_128-0) *[Star Wars: Timelines](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Timelines "Star Wars: Timelines")* dates the events of "[Chapter 1: The Mandalorian](/wiki/Chapter_1:_The_Mandalorian "Chapter 1: The Mandalorian")" of [*The Mandalorian* Season One](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_Season_One "The Mandalorian Season One") to [9 ABY](/wiki/9_ABY "9 ABY"). In addition, [SWInsider](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider "Star Wars Insider") "[A Certain Point of View](/wiki/A_Certain_Point_of_View_(department) "A Certain Point of View (department)")" — [*Star Wars Insider* 228](/wiki/Star_Wars_Insider_228 "Star Wars Insider 228") also dates "[Part Seven: Dreams and Madness](/wiki/Part_Seven:_Dreams_and_Madness "Part Seven: Dreams and Madness")" to nine [years](/wiki/Standard_year "Standard year") after the events of [*Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope*](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_IV_A_New_Hope "Star Wars: Episode IV A New Hope"), which corresponds to 9 [ABY](/wiki/%27ABY-BBY%27_dating_system "'ABY-BBY' dating system") per *Timelines*. "Part Seven: Dreams and Madness" takes place after the [liberation of Mandalore](/wiki/Liberation_of_Mandalore "Liberation of Mandalore"), which is the main event depicted in "[Chapter 23: The Spies](/wiki/Chapter_23:_The_Spies "Chapter 23: The Spies")" and "[Chapter 24: The Return](/wiki/Chapter_24:_The_Return "Chapter 24: The Return")," the final two episodes of [*The Mandalorian* Season Three](/wiki/The_Mandalorian_Season_Three "The Mandalorian Season Three"). Therefore, Seasons One through Three of *[Star Wars: The Mandalorian](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Mandalorian "Star Wars: The Mandalorian")* must all be set in 9 ABY as well. [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com") [SWCA 2022: 20 Highlights from Lucasfilm's Studio Showcase](https://www.starwars.com/news/swca-2022-20-highlights-from-lucasfilms-studio-showcase) on [StarWars.com](/wiki/StarWars.com "StarWars.com") ([backup link](https://web.archive.org/web/20220527003823/https://www.starwars.com/news/swca-2022-20-highlights-from-lucasfilms-studio-showcase)) states that *[Star Wars: Skeleton Crew](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Skeleton_Crew "Star Wars: Skeleton Crew")* takes place in the same timeframe as *[Star Wars: The Mandalorian](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Mandalorian "Star Wars: The Mandalorian")* and *[Star Wars: Ahsoka](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Ahsoka "Star Wars: Ahsoka")*—the latter of which can also be dated to 9 ABY following the reasoning [here](/wiki/Template:AhsokaSeriesDate "Template:AhsokaSeriesDate"). As such, *Skeleton Crew* must take place around 9 ABY as well. 129.
